# Continuation Prompt — TI-84 Plus CE ROM Transpilation

> ⚠ **Auto-continuation loop active** — Windows Task Scheduler `TI84-AutoContinuation` fires a headless Opus session every 1h (daily trigger at midnight, then hourly repeat). Before editing this file in a human session, check `git log --oneline` for recent `auto-session N` commits and consider `schtasks /change /tn "TI84-AutoContinuation" /disable` to prevent conflicts. Re-enable with `/enable`. Change interval: `schtasks /change /tn "TI84-AutoContinuation" /ri <minutes>`. Launcher: `scripts/auto-continuation.bat`. Logs: `logs/auto-session-*.log` (gitignored).

**Last updated**: 2026-04-30 (session 160 — Phase 25CM: 3 sub-priorities completed. **KEY FINDINGS**: (1) **CALL AT 0x07C74B → 0x07CA48 CONFIRMED CORRECT** — P1 static disassembly verified ROM bytes at 0x07C74B = `CD 48 CA 07` (CALL 0x07CA48). Transpilation target is correct, not the source of the gcd bug. 7 callers of 0x07CA48 found (1 JP via JT 0x0201EC + 6 CALL sites). (2) **0x07CA48 IS A PURE NORMALIZATION ROUTINE WITH NO INTEGER EXTRACTION** — Full 88-byte disassembly: loops Shl14+DecExp until exp < 0x80, then combines OP1/OP2 exponents via ADD + sign XOR → RET at 0x07CA9F. Zero stores of shifted-out mantissa digits. The mantissa destruction is TOTAL and by design — this function is meant for exponent combination, not value preservation. (3) **ALL INPUTS WITH EXP >= 0x80 GET MANTISSA DESTROYED** — P2 tested 4 inputs: 12.0 (exp=0x81, 2 shifts→zeroed), 8.0 (exp=0x80, 1 shift→zeroed), 1200 (exp=0x83, 4 shifts→zeroed), 1.0 (exp=0x80, 1 shift→zeroed). Even the ORIGINAL gcd values without the +2 exponent bump are destroyed. Shift count = exp - 0x7F. OP2 is NEVER modified by 0x07CA48. (4) **OP1TOOP2 AT 0x07C747 IS A COMPOUND FUNCTION, NOT JUST A COPY** — P3 dynamic trace reveals: 0x07C747 does CALL 0x07F8FA (OP1→OP2 copy) → CALL 0x07CA48 (normalize OP1, destroys mantissa) → CALL **0x07CA06** (unknown JT entry) → JR 0x07C77F (FPAdd entry). After normalization returns with OP1=0, execution calls 0x07CA06 then enters FPAdd. The gcd's "OP1toOP2" actually feeds into FP addition/subtraction, NOT division. **MAJOR ARCHITECTURAL INSIGHT**: The 0x07C747 variant includes normalization; variant at 0x07C755 does OP1→OP2 copy WITHOUT normalization then JR to FPAdd directly. Multiple entry points exist: 0x07C75B (load 1.0 + add), 0x07C767 (+ sub), 0x07C76D (load 1.0 + sub). The gcd handler calls 0x07C747 (WITH normalization), which may be the WRONG entry for integer arithmetic. **CRITICAL NEXT**: Disassemble 0x07CA06 (the function called AFTER normalization returns). It's a JT entry at 0x0201E4. Understanding what it does with the zeroed OP1 and preserved OP2 is the key to understanding whether normalization is intentional or a wrong-entry-point bug. Seeds: 50,058. Blocks: 143,616. Covered: 699,830. Codex: not dispatched (stalled since session 96). Sonnet: 3/3 completed and verified by Opus. Golden regression 26/26 PASS.) Prior session 156 — Phase 25CI: 3 sub-priorities of FPDiv/gcd investigation completed. **MAJOR FINDINGS**: (1) **FPDiv IMPLEMENTATION IS CORRECT** — FPDiv(12,8)=1.5 and FPDiv(1200,1200)=1.0 both produce correct results when entering impl at 0x07CAB9 directly (202 and 185 steps respectively). The gcd E_Domain bug is NOT a FPDiv core algorithm issue. (2) **FPDiv JT SLOT 0x0201F4 IS A MISSING BLOCK** — needs transpiler seed. Falls through to 0x0201F8 (SqRoot). Session 154's "confirmed working via JT slot" must have used the impl directly. (3) **0x07F8B6 = OP4→OP2 COPY, NOT FPDiv CHAIN** — session 155's claim that "0x07F8B6 chains into FP computation at 0x07CA48" was WRONG. 0x07F8B6 is a 9-byte Mov9 stub: `LD HL,0xD00619; LD DE,0xD00603; JP 0x07F974`. (4) **OP REGISTER NAMING CORRECTION** — what sessions 153-155 called "OP3" at 0xD00624 is actually **OP5** per ti84pceg.inc (OP3=0xD0060E, OP4=0xD00619, OP5=0xD00624). The gcd backup register is OP5. (5) **OP5 IS ACTIVELY USED IN GCD** — 2 writes (steps 185, 896) at PC=0x068D91 (OP1→OP5 backup), 2 reads (steps 570, 1274) at PC=0x07F8D8 (OP5→OP2 restore). Algorithm runs 2 iterations. Final: OP5=100 (positive), OP1=OP2=-100 (sign-corrupted). 144 ROM references to OP5 range found. **ROOT CAUSE REFINED**: The gcd algorithm enters FP computation via 0x07CA48 (normalization pre-loop), NOT via FPDiv JT slot or impl. The normalization loop shifts mantissa left + decrements exponent until exp<0x80, destroying the mantissa for high-exponent inputs. **NEXT**: Trace the EXACT code path from 0x07CA48 during gcd(12,8) — what are OP1/OP2 when this function is entered, and how does the normalization loop feed into the actual division? The entry context (not FPDiv impl) is the bug site. Codex: 3/3 stalled (0 bytes). Sonnet: 4/4 completed and verified by Opus. Golden regression 26/26 PASS. Covered bytes: 699,826 (95.93%). Seeds: 50,057. Blocks: 143,615.) Prior session 149 — Phase 25CB: 2 priorities completed. (1) **GCD SIGN CORRUPTION FULLY TRACED — 0x07C753 IS FP SUBTRACTION SIGN-SET, 0x068D59 IS TERMINAL CORRUPTION, TYPE VALIDATOR ALWAYS CLEAN (P1, KEY FINDING)**: Step-by-step OP1/OP2 trace across all 1442 gcd steps. 0x07C753 sets OP1[0]=0x80 (sign bit) 4 times during Euclidean loop (steps 199/582/910/1286) — FP subtraction helper. Each time REPAIRED by 0x07FA86 (1.0 constant loader resets to 0x00). Type validator at 0x07F831 hit 4 times (steps 21/353/740/1064) — ALWAYS sees clean 0x00 type bytes. **TERMINAL CORRUPTION**: step 1428 at 0x07C783 corrupts OP2[0]→0x80 (never repaired); step 1439 at 0x068D59 corrupts OP1[0]→0x80 (never repaired). Both happen AFTER the last type validator check. The gcd algorithm's final iteration leaves sign bits set because the repair routine (0x07FA86) is not called post-loop. **0x80 = negative Real sign bit, NOT invalid type code.** The Euclidean loop computes correctly but the sign-cleanup at loop exit is missing. NEXT: (a) disassemble 0x068D59 to understand what it does (likely stores subtraction result with sign bit), (b) check if the gcd algorithm expects a final ABS or type-byte-mask step after the loop that we're missing, (c) test: manually clear OP1[0] and OP2[0] to 0x00 before the type validator and see if gcd returns 4.0. (2) **IPOINT FLAG SWEEP — 16 COMBINATIONS, 0 VRAM WRITES, VRAM ADDRESS CORRECT (P2, ELIMINATES FLAG HYPOTHESIS)**: Tested all 16 combinations of 4 IY flags (IY+0x3C bit 0, IY+0x02 bit 1, IY+0x2B bit 2, IY+0x4A bit 2). IY+2B bit 2 is the only flag that matters — when SET, stored VRAM pointer at 0xD02A8A reads 0xD52AC0 (correct for Y=120, X=160), steps increase from 14 to ~40-45. All other flags have zero effect. **NO combination writes any VRAM bytes.** plotSScreen gets 28-32 bytes of side-effect traffic in all cases. The pixel store instruction (`LD (BC),A` at 0x07B682) is not executing. **HYPOTHESIS**: The issue is NOT the IY flag combination — it's likely (a) a runtime-level issue (cpu-runtime.js write handling in VRAM range), (b) the pixel-write instruction is gated by an additional condition not in these 4 flags, or (c) the NZ path through 0x07B682 needs a different code path to be taken. Session 129 DID get pixel writes (drawMode=1, IY+43 SET, IY+74 CLEAR) — the difference may be in how session 129's probe set up the calling context vs. how session 149 set registers. Handler table at 0x068580-0x0685AA has two regions: 0x068580-0x06859A uses JR to common `CALL 0x096024` dispatch (categories 0x00-0x0F), while 0x06859B-0x0685A9 uses `CALL 0x0689DE` which does `SUB 0x20` then indexes jump table at 0x0689F9 via `JP (HL)` (categories 0x28-0x2A). (3) **BUFINSERT CALLING CONVENTION CORRECTED (MAJOR FIX)**: Session 130's +2 stride and metadata bytes were caused by WRONG REGISTER — BufInsert takes token in **DE** (E=token, D=two-byte flag), NOT BC. The routine does PUSH DE first, CALL room-check, POP BC — the POP overwrites BC with the saved DE value. With correct convention (token in E, D=0): cursor advances +1 per token (not +2), buffer stores raw token bytes `32 70 33` = "2+3", each insertion completes in 7 steps (not 12). Z path → checks numLastEntries → if 0 JP 0x058C65 ("empty ENTER" cleanup) → if nonzero recalls last entry → JR 0x058693. BOTH paths converge at 0x058693 (common tail) which includes: CALL 0x082961, CALL 0x09215E, CALL 0x0A27DD, then **CALL 0x099910 at 0x0586E3**. 0x099910 is a 4-byte trampoline: `CALL 0x07FF81` then falls through to ParseInp at 0x099914. ---

## ★ Strategic Reframing (READ FIRST)

**The 16.65% "plateau" is a denominator artifact**, not a reachability problem. ROM is 4 MB but **82.6% (3,464,815 bytes) is erased flash (0xFF fill)** — fundamentally uncoverable. The genuine executable+data ROM is **729,489 non-erased bytes**, and the transpiler already covers **95.92% of them**.

Of the remaining ~30 KB of uncovered non-erased bytes:

| Verdict | Bytes | % |
|---------|-------|---|
| CODE? (decodable) | ~13 KB | 29% |
| DATA-MIXED | ~24 KB | 52% |
| DATA-SPARSE | ~6 KB | 13% |
| STRINGS | ~3 KB | 6% |

Only ~13 KB is plausibly executable code, scattered across ~3,400 tiny ranges (top hole = 62 bytes). **Coverage work is effectively done.** Future sessions should pivot to feature work. Use `audit-true-uncovered.mjs` for true coverage, not `coveragePercent`.

---

## Current State

- **True coverage**: 95.93% (699,830 / 729,489 non-erased bytes)
- **Reported coverage**: 16.69% (143,616 blocks)
- **Seed count**: 50,058
- **Live stubs**: 0. **OS jump table**: 980/980. **ISR dispatch gate**: unlocked.
- **Keyboard scan, ISR dispatch, VRAM pipeline, OS init, real boot, home-screen render**: all working end-to-end.
- **Golden regression** (`node TI-84_Plus_CE/probe-phase99d-home-verify.mjs`): 26/26 exact at row 39 col 2, "Normal Float Radian" 3/3 PASS, status dots PASS (36 fg pixels), total 1004 fg pixels.
- `ROM.transpiled.js` gitignored (~214 MB). `.gz` committed (~16 MB, regenerate with `gzip -k -9 ROM.transpiled.js`).
- **Per-stage IX convention**: home-screen stages 1–4 all need `IX = 0xD1A860` before entry. Stage 3 exit IX = `0xe00800`, others = `0x0159bd`. Don't use `IX = SP` (crashes stages 1/4 at 0x58c35b).
- **Display buffer 0xD006C0 has no natural OS populator**. Browser-shell seeds it via restore path 0x088720 (seed 260 bytes into backup buffer 0xD02EC7, then call 0x088720).

## Next-Session Priorities

> **Status update (2026-04-30, session 160)**: Session 160 completed 3 sub-priorities. **KEY ARCHITECTURAL INSIGHT**: OP1toOP2 at 0x07C747 is a COMPOUND function (copy + normalize + CALL 0x07CA06 + FPAdd), NOT just a copy. The gcd handler calls this compound variant, which may be the wrong entry point. 0x07CA06 (JT entry at 0x0201E4) is the unknown function called after normalization destroys OP1. Multiple OP1toOP2 variants exist with/without normalization. 0x07CA48 is confirmed a pure normalization with NO integer extraction — mantissa destruction is total for ALL exp >= 0x80 inputs.

### 1. ★★★ FP gcd — Disassemble 0x07CA06 (post-normalization function) and determine if gcd should use 0x07C755 instead
Session 160 established: (a) CALL at 0x07C74B → 0x07CA48 is CONFIRMED CORRECT in ROM bytes — not a transpilation error. (b) 0x07CA48 has 7 callers and is a legitimate JT entry for exponent combination + sign XOR. (c) ALL inputs with exp >= 0x80 get mantissa zeroed (including 8.0 and 12.0 without the +2 bump). (d) After normalization returns (OP1=0, OP2=preserved), 0x07C74F calls 0x07CA06 then JR to 0x07C77F (FPAdd). **CRITICAL NEXT STEPS**: (a) **Disassemble 0x07CA06** — it's the unknown function at JT slot 0x0201E4, called after normalization. What does it do with zeroed OP1 and preserved OP2? Does it restore OP1 from somewhere, or does it perform the actual division/multiplication using the combined exponent? This is the #1 unknown blocking gcd root cause resolution. (b) **Check the JT name for 0x0201E4** — look up in `phase25h-a-jump-table.json` or ti84pceg.inc to see if this function has a known name. (c) **Compare gcd call to 0x07C747 vs 0x07C755** — the gcd handler at 0x068D61 calls 0x07C747 (with normalize). Would calling 0x07C755 (copy WITHOUT normalize, then FPAdd) produce correct results? Test by intercepting 0x068D61's CALL target. (d) **Trace the SECOND normalization call** — P3 showed that after the first OP1toOP2 (step 58-171), at step 190 OP1=1200 again with full mantissa. How? Something between FPAdd at 0x07C77F and the next OP1toOP2 at step 446 restored OP1. Trace those intermediate steps to understand the full Euclidean loop flow. Key probes: `probe-phase160-07c74b-disasm.mjs` (P1), `probe-phase160-norm-inputs.mjs` (P2), `probe-phase160-op1toop2-flow.mjs` (P3).

Step 1: OP1=12.0, OP2=8.0, FPS=0xD1AA12. Step 18 (ConstLoader): 8.0 pushed to FPS (0xD1AA12→0xD1AA1B), OP2 overwritten with 1.0. Step 21 (TypeValidator): OP1=12.0, OP2=1.0. Steps 171-200: FPAdd/SubCore calls with OP2=[00 83 12 00...] — algorithm uses exponent 0x83 (10^3 scaling) for integer extraction. **Step 353 (TypeValidator): OP1=0, OP2=8.0.** First mod result is 0, NOT 4. Expected: 12 mod 8 = 4. The INT(a/b) division between steps 21-171 is producing the wrong quotient. Steps 740/1064: ConstLoader fires again, loop continues with wrong intermediate values. Steps 1422-1442: FPS_dec9, FPSub, gcdTailJP, final OP1=OP2=[80 82 10 00...]=(-10.0), errNo=0x84. Hit counts: SubCore×11, FPAdd×10, TypeValidator×4, ConstLoader×2, FPS_dec9×2, gcdEntry×1, FPSub×1, gcdTailJP×1. **NEXT**: Trace all blocks between steps 21-171 to find where INT(12/8) goes wrong — is OP2 still 1.0 at division time (meaning the pop happens too late) or does it reload 8.0 from FPS? Sonnet P1: completed and verified by Opus. Codex P1: stalled (0 bytes). Golden regression 26/26 PASS.
- ✅ **Phase 25CE — IPOINT 16BPP COLOR MECHANISM FULLY DECODED + 4/4 COLOR TESTS PASS (P2, CLOSES INVESTIGATION + CORRECTS SESSION 151)**: Built `probe-phase152-ipoint-color-fix.mjs`. **Part A (disassembly 0x07B5B6→0x07B682)**: Block 0x07B5B6 = `BIT 7,(IY+30); JR NZ,0x07B62B` — conditional jump to color-decision block. Block 0x07B62B = `PUSH AF; POP AF; OR A; LD DE,(mbase<<16|0x26AC); JR NZ,0x07B677` — loads drawFGColor (16-bit) into DE, uses A (drawMode) only as boolean (NZ = draw, Z = erase). Block 0x07B677 = `LD BC,(0xD02A8A)` — loads VRAM pointer. Block 0x07B682 = **`LD A,E; LD (BC),A`** — writes drawFGColor LOW byte (NOT drawMode as session 151 claimed). `LD A,E` REPLACES drawMode in A with drawFGColor_lo. Block 0x07B68A = `INC BC; LD A,D; LD (BC),A` — writes drawFGColor HIGH byte. **Session 151's claim "first pixel byte = drawMode" was WRONG** — A=0x01 at block entry gets replaced by `LD A,E` before the store. Session 151 saw VRAM=0x01 because drawFGColor was 0x0000 (E=0x00 → stored 0x00, not the A=0x01 drawMode). **Part B (4-color test)**: Blue (drawFGColor=0x001F): VRAM=[0x1F, 0x00] ✓. Red (0xF800): VRAM=[0x00, 0xF8] ✓. Green (0x07E0): VRAM=[0xE0, 0x07] ✓. White (0xFFFF): VRAM=[0xFF, 0xFF] ✓. All match drawFGColor in little-endian BGR565. **Part C (encoding analysis)**: 16bpp pixel = drawFGColor stored LE as [E=fgLo, D=fgHi]. Only 2 bytes per pixel (bytes 3-4 remain sentinel). drawMode is used purely as a boolean gate (NZ→draw, Z→erase). drawColorCode (0xD026AE) is used only by 8bpp plotSScreen Z-path, not the 16bpp LCD VRAM NZ-path. VRAM address uses inverted Y: (0xEF-C)×0xA0×2, not naive Y×640. **IPOINT COLOR INVESTIGATION IS CLOSED.** For colored graph pixels: seed drawFGColor at 0xD026AC with BGR565 value before IPoint call. Sonnet P2: completed and verified by Opus. Codex P2: stalled (0 bytes). Golden regression 26/26 PASS.

- ✅ **Phase 25CC — GCD SIGN FIX — VALIDATOR-INTERCEPT APPROACH CONFIRMED WRONG, FIX MUST BE POST-LOOP (P1, KEY CORRECTION)**: Built `probe-phase150-gcd-signfix.mjs`. **Part A (Quick Test)**: Intercepted all 4 type validator hits (0x07F831) at steps 21/353/740/1064. The corruption happens AFTER the last validator call (step 1064) at steps 1428 (0x07C783→OP2) and 1439 (0x068D59→OP1). **CONCLUSION**: The type validator cannot prevent the corruption — the fix must intercept AFTER the loop exits. **Part B (Disassembly)**: 0x068D59 = single instruction `JP 0x082912`. Target 0x082912 = FPS dec-9 helper: `LD BC,0x000009; LD HL,(0xD0258D); OR A; SBC HL,BC; JR 0x08292B`. 0x07C783 = `RES 6,(IY+14)` then `CALL 0x07CC36` — the CALL 0x07CC36 is the FP subtraction that produces sign corruption in OP2. Block 0x07C77F (alternate containing 0x07C783): `SET 6,(IY+89); RES 6,(IY+14); CALL 0x07CC36` — this is FPAdd entry (0x07C77F = FPAdd JT slot). - ✅ **Phase 25CB — GCD SIGN CORRUPTION FULLY TRACED — 0x07C753 IS FP SUBTRACTION SIGN-SET, 0x068D59 IS TERMINAL CORRUPTION (P1, KEY FINDING)**: Built `probe-phase149-gcd-sign-trace.mjs`. Step-by-step OP1/OP2 snapshot at every block across 1442 gcd steps. **OP1[0] transitions**: 0x07C753 sets sign bit (0x00→0x80) 4 times (steps 199/582/910/1286) — this is the FP subtraction helper. Each corruption repaired by 0x07FA86 (steps 242/625/953/1329) which is the 1.0 constant loader resetting type byte to 0x00. **Terminal corruption**: step 1428 at 0x07C783 sets OP2[0]→0x80 (NEVER repaired). Step 1439 at 0x068D59 sets OP1[0]→0x80 (NEVER repaired — this is INSIDE the gcd handler). Both happen AFTER the last type validator check (step 1064). **Type validator (0x07F831)**: Hit 4 times at steps 21/353/740/1064. ALWAYS sees OP1[0]=0x00 and OP2[0]=0x00 — clean type bytes during loop body. The validator is NOT the problem — the sign corruption happens post-loop. **0x80 = negative Real sign bit** (bit 7 of type byte), NOT an invalid type code. Context around first corruption: steps 194-204 show 0x07CA0E→0x07CA14→0x07FD4A→0x07CA18→0x07CA20→**0x07C753** (sign set)→0x07C77F (FPAdd entry). This is the subtraction-via-negation path in the FP library. Final FPS ptr: 0xD1AA24 (grew from 0xD1AA00 base during loop, then decreased via real pops). Sonnet P1: completed and verified by Opus. Golden regression 26/26 PASS.
- ✅ **Phase 25CB — IPOINT 16-FLAG COMBINATION SWEEP — 0 VRAM WRITES, ELIMINATES IY FLAG HYPOTHESIS (P2, KEY FINDING)**: Built `probe-phase149-ipoint-flags.mjs`. Tested all 16 combinations of 4 IY flags: IY+0x3C bit 0 (SET/CLR), IY+0x02 bit 1 (SET/CLR), IY+0x2B bit 2 (SET/CLR), IY+0x4A bit 2 (SET/CLR). Target pixel: C=120 (Y), DE=160 (X), drawMode=1. **Results**: IY+2B bit 2 (IY+43) is the ONLY flag that changes behavior — when SET, stored VRAM pointer at 0xD02A8A correctly reads 0xD52AC0, steps increase from 14 to ~40-45. All other flags (IY+3C, IY+02, IY+4A) have ZERO measurable effect on VRAM writes or VRAM pointer. **NO combination of 16 wrote any VRAM bytes.** plotSScreen gets 28-32 bytes of side-effect traffic in all cases (stack/scratch overlap, not pixel data). The VRAM address computation is correct (0xD52AC0 for Y=120, X=160) but the pixel store instruction does not execute. **CONCLUSION**: The issue is NOT in the IY flag combination — it's either (a) a runtime-level write handling issue in the VRAM range, (b) an additional condition not in these 4 flags, or (c) a calling-context difference vs. session 129 which DID get pixel writes. Sonnet P2: completed and verified by Opus. Golden regression 26/26 PASS.

For function mode: table_base_L=0x10. With A=0: (0-1)+0x10 = 0xFF+0x10 = 0x0F (WRONG). With A=1: 0+0x10 = 0x10 = tY1 (CORRECT). OP1 becomes [0x03, 0x5E, 0x0F, ...] → ChkFindSym fails → ERR:UNDEFINED at step 71. **GraphPars NEVER reaches token evaluation or ParseInp.** Parser pointer pre-seeding (Test B) had ZERO effect — error is before any parser state matters. **Fix options**: (a) call body entry 0x099874 with OP1=[0x03, 0x10, 0x00...], (b) seed equation iteration index RAM variable, (c) use higher-level graph entry that sets up iteration context. **PushErrorHandler architecture mapped**: recovery at 0x0998CA, error codes > 8 (AND 0x7F) re-thrown via JP 0x061DB6. First instruction is `PUSH DE`, then `CALL room-check` (0x05E3D6), then `POP BC` — this POP overwrites BC with the saved DE value. Prior sessions passed token in BC, which was clobbered by POP → garbage bytes (pointer metadata from whatever was in DE) and +2 stride (non-zero D triggered two-byte path). **With correct convention (E=token, D=0)**: cursor advances +1 per token, buffer stores raw token bytes `32 70 33` = "2+3", 7 steps per insertion. Room-check at 0x05E3D6 loads editCursor (0xD0243A) and editTail (0xD0243D), compares via SBC at 0x0CC973. CreateNumEditBuf (0x096E09) confirmed NOT initializing pointers — manual init works. Key-to-token conversion uses cascading CP/JP dispatch at 0x045C37 (not single indexed table); digit keys k0-k9 (0x8E-0x97) likely convert via `token = kCode - 0x8E + 0x30`. Sonnet P3. Golden regression 26/26 PASS.

LCD mem-patching (RET at 0x001221) ineffective — transpiled blocks execute pre-compiled JS, not memory bytes. Sonnet P1.
- ✅ **Phase 25BH — IPoint WORKS: PIXELS WRITTEN TO plotSScreen (P2, MAJOR MILESTONE)**: Built `probe-phase129-graph-render.mjs` with 5 scenarios. **drawMode=1 (normal draw) at coordinates (10,10) → 1 pixel written to plotSScreen[0x1B8E]=0xF0 in 47 steps. drawMode=2 (XOR) also writes pixels (53 steps).** Root causes of prior failures identified: (a) drawMode=0 = ERASE (OS DECrements A internally; A=0→DEC→0xFF→erase path writes color 0x00 = invisible on empty buffer). Correct draw mode is A=1. (b) Bounds-check at 0x07B793 requires seeded pixWideP (0xD014FE, 16-bit width) and pixWide_m_2 (0xD01501, 16-bit height) — with zeros, ALL coordinates fail. X bounds use 8-bit `CP L` comparison — coordinates ≥ low byte of pixWideP fail (e.g., with pixWideP=320, L=0x40, so X≥64 fails). MBASE confirmed 0xD0 at bounds-check in all scenarios. RAM seeding map: 0xD014FE=width, 0xD01501=height, 0xD026AE=pen color (2 bytes), 0xD000B5 bit 7=0 (hookflags3). Pixel write mechanism at 0x07B7CC: loads pen color from 0xD02A60, computes plotSScreen offset, writes nibble. Sonnet P2.
- ✅ **Phase 25BH — EDIT BUFFER SYSTEM FULLY MAPPED (P3, RESEARCH)**: Built `probe-phase129-edit-buffer.mjs`. **Edit buffer = gap buffer**: editTop=0xD02437, editCursor=0xD0243A, editTail=0xD0243D, editBtm=0xD02440 (all 24-bit pointers). editSym=0xD0244E, editDat=0xD02451. **OS routines resolved**: BufClr→0x0ADAC3 (returned 351 steps but didn't init pointers — needs pre-initialized buffer), BufInsert→0x05E2A0 (token in C/BC, calls 0x05E3D6 room check, updates editCursor at 0xD0243A), BufDelete→0x05E367, BufLeft→0x05E242, BufRight→0x05E27E, CreateNumEditBuf→0x096E09 (likely the actual initializer). **Key codes corrected**: k0=0x8E through k9=0x97 (NOT scan codes). Scan-to-key table at 0x09F79B confirmed: sk2=0x1A → table[0x1A] = 0x90 = k2. **Home handler stalls**: With cxCurApp=0x40, kbdKey=0x90, handler at 0x058241 enters 0x08BF22 (CoorMon yield) → stalls at 0x09EFDE (MMIO busy-wait for LCD/timer, 6528 hits in 50K steps). Never reaches BufInsert. Next: call CreateNumEditBuf to init, then BufInsert directly. Sonnet P3.
- Golden regression 26/26 PASS (bestMatch=row39 col2, Normal/Float/Radian 3/3, status dots PASS). Codex: not dispatched (stalling since session 96). Sonnet: 3/3 completed and verified by Opus.

- ✅ **Phase 25BG — 0xBB DISPATCH CHAIN FULLY TRACED + ROOT CAUSE FOUND (P3, KEY FINDING)**: Built `probe-phase128-bb-dispatch.mjs`. ParseInp correctly dispatches 0xBB-prefix tokens — for min(3,7), it parses first argument (OP1=3.0, curPC advances from 0xD00800 to 0xD00805, consuming 5 of 7 bytes). Execution proceeds through 0x066436→0x07F95E→0x07F974→0x066445→0x07F7D6→...→0x061D2C→0x061DB2 (JError)→0x03E1B4→0x0011DA→0x001221 (LCD busy-wait). **ROOT CAUSE**: Operation code 0xDA (min's internal FP operation) is not in the FP comparison dispatch table at 0x0686D3. The dispatch table handles known FP ops but 0xDA falls through → error → JError → LCD output → LCD busy-wait polling loop at 0x001229/0x00122D (infinite). OPS dump shows 0xDA at 0xD3FFF8. Added 8 seeds for LCD path blocks in `phase128bb-seeds.txt` (0x0011DA, 0x001200, 0x001213, 0x001221, 0x001228, 0x001239, 0x001242, 0x001249). Sonnet P3.

### Completed (session 127)
- ✅ **Phase 25BF — POST-PARSEINP ALLOCATOR LOOP SOLVED (P1, KEY FINDING)**: Built `probe-phase127-post-parseinp.mjs` with 2 scenarios. **Scenario 1 (re-seed + continue)**: After ParseInp("2+3") returns OP1=5.0 (919 steps), dumped allocator state: OPS=0xD40002 (overflowed 3 bytes past OPBase=0xD3FFFF), FPS=0xD1A878 (underflowed 9 bytes below FPSbase=0xD1A881). Re-seeded OPBase/OPS/FPS/pTemp/progPtr to post-MEM_INIT values, then continued from 0x05822A (first post-ParseInp call). Result: **returned to FAKE_RET in just 2 steps**, zero allocator loop hits, OP1=5.0 preserved. 0x05822A is a missing block in the transpiled code → falls through immediately. **Scenario 2 (skip cleanup)**: OP1=5.0 intact after ParseInp with no cleanup needed. **KEY FINDING**: The post-ParseInp allocator loop was caused solely by OPS overflow corruption. Re-seeding pointers after ParseInp eliminates it entirely. The full common-tail round-trip (0x0586CE → ParseInp → cleanup → FAKE_RET) is now achievable with pointer re-seeding. Sonnet P1.
- ✅ **Phase 25BF — TWO-BYTE TOKEN MAP EXTENDED (P3)**: Extended `browser-shell.html` with 12 new tokens. Added `EVAL_TWO_BYTE_TOKENS` array sorted longest-first for prefix-safe matching. Tokenizer emits [0xBB, secondByte] for two-byte functions. Probe 1/4 PASS: 8*8*8=512 ✓ (control). min(3,7), max(3,7), gcd(12,8) all stall/fail at PC=0x001221 — ROM's 0xBB-prefix dispatch not fully lifted (ROM coverage gap, not tokenizer bug — byte sequences verified correct). Golden regression 26/26 PASS. Sonnet P3.
- ✅ **Phase 25BF — GRAPH IPoint/ILine CALLING CONVENTIONS DECODED + .SIS PREFIX BLOCKER (P2, KEY FINDING)**: Built `probe-phase127-graph-render.mjs`. Disassembled IPoint (0x07B451) and ILine (0x07B245) statically and traced execution. **IPoint**: A=draw mode → 0xD02AC8, mode byte 0 → 0xD02AD4, checks BIT 7,(IY+35h) then BIT 5,(IY+14h), main path at 0x07B504 loads pen color from 0xD026AE, calls bounds-check at 0x07B793. **ILine**: A=draw mode, mode byte 1 → 0xD02AD4, saves BC/DE to 0xD022D1/D2, computes deltas, calls division at 0x04C979, iteratively calls IPoint. **BLOCKER FOUND**: Bounds-check at 0x07B793 uses eZ80 .SIS prefix (opcode 0x40) before `LD HL,(nn)`. Transpiler treats 0x40 as `LD B,B` (Z80 compat) → reads wrong 3-byte address 0xB71501 instead of intended 2-byte 0x1501+MBASE → garbage → bounds check fails → bail-out before any pixel-writing code. **FIX**: Implement .SIS/.LIS/.SIL/.LIL prefix handling (opcodes 0x40/0x49/0x52/0x5B) in ez80-decoder.js and transpiler. No pixels written to plotSScreen (expected given the blocker). Sonnet P2.

## Research-Informed Refinements (added 2026-04-24 from external deep-research pass)

Grounded in TI-83 Plus SDK prose (parser/error-handler contracts), WikiTI 83+ memory-layout page, and the CE include mirror (ti84pceg.inc). Public record has **zero labels** for 0x099211 / 0x099910 / 0x07FF81 / 0x08BF22 / 0x0831A4 / 0x09215E / 0x04C940 — our RE is the source of truth on those. Highlights that inform current priorities:

### R1. ✅ RESOLVED (session 110) — `pTempCnt` audit
pTempCnt at 0xD02596 is correctly zeroed by MEM_INIT (confirmed 0x000000). Stays zero throughout MEM_INIT → CreateReal → ParseInp pipeline and across all expression evaluations. NOT a factor in the RclVarSym failure.

### R2. ✅ RESOLVED (session 111) — Parser flags fully enumerated
Report flags these publicly-named knobs as likely ParseInp-sensitive (all from CE include):
- `ParsFlag`, `ParsFlag2` (including `numOP1` = "result in OP1")
- `onFlags.parseInput`
- `fmtFlags`, `numMode`, `fmtOverride`
- `graphFlags2.splitOverride`
- `newDispF.allowProgTokens`, `progExecuting`
- `hookflags4.parserHookActive` + `parserHookPtr`

**Action**: enumerate each against postInitState. Current probes may accidentally inherit a clean zero-state that works, but any leftover bit from a prior CoorMon iteration would silently change ParseInp's branch. Deterministic seed = deterministic trace.

### R3. ✅ RESOLVED (session 110) — Descending-boundary invariant
Invariant holds after MEM_INIT and after CreateReal, but **VIOLATED after ParseInp** in ALL cases:
- `FPSbase > FPS` (FPS underflows 9 bytes below base — one 9-byte FP value pushed downward)
- `OPS > OPBase` (OPS overflows 6-12 bytes above base — operator stack grows upward past boundary)
This is the root cause of VAT entry corruption (priority 1). ParseInp does not clean up FPS/OPS after evaluation — the OS normally handles this between stages.

### R4. ✅ RESOLVED (session 110) — 0x099211 is NOT ParseInpGraph
Static disassembly of 300 bytes confirms: 0x099211 is a "DisarmScroll" / variable-recall-to-edit-buffer routine. No CALL/JP to ParseInp (0x099914), no trampoline reference (0x099910), no PushErrorHandler (0x061DEF), and ZERO IY ops in the ParsFlag area (IY+0x44 through IY+0x4C). All 8 IY operations target lower offsets (statFlags at IY+0x09, IY+0x01, IY+0x05). Session 98's "DisarmScroll" name was correct. The ParseInpGraph hypothesis is disproved for this address.

### R5. ★ Treat `errSP` as RAM snapshot, not live SP (mental model fix)
TI's 83+ `ResetStacks` comment is explicit: `(onsp)→(errsp), (fpbase)→(fps), (opbase)→(ops)`. `errSP` is a RAM-saved snapshot distinct from the hardware SP. Our session-108 18-byte frame-pop finding is reverse-engineered behavior (TI only publishes "six pushes" + SP/FPS/OPS restore), so brittle by design. Implication: when diagnosing trampoline/SP-shift issues, track `errSP` (RAM) and `SP` (CPU) as **two independent state variables** and log both in error-path probes.

- ✅ **Phase 25BB — DIRECT-EVAL TOKEN MAPPING EXTENDED (P1)**: Extended `EVAL_TOKEN_MAP` with 50+ new entries: scientific notation E (0x3B), power ^ (0x0F), comma (0x2B), π (0xAC), A-Z uppercase (0x41-0x5A), a-z lowercase (same tokens, 'e' unmapped). Added multi-character token matching: Ans, sin, cos, tan, ln, log, sqrt, abs, e^, plus √ unicode. Added whitespace skipping. Updated negation context for comma, ^, and function tokens. Codex P1 did bulk mapping; Sonnet P1 added negation triggers. Golden regression 26/26 PASS.
- ✅ **Phase 25BB — RCLVARSYM APPROACH B BOUNDARY CHECK ROOT CAUSE (P2)**: Built `probe-phase25bb-rclvarsym-disasm.mjs` with block-by-block trace comparison. **EXACT DIVERGENCE**: Step 8 at PC=0x084716 — FindSym compares DE against HL=0xD3FFF9 (stale boundary from default OPBase). Scenario A: DE=0xD3FFEE < limit → found. Scenario B: DE=0xD4004F > limit → carry → error path → copies from HL=0xFFFFAA → garbage OP1. NOT an off-by-N error — it's a stale boundary limit never updated for non-default OPBase. Approach B definitively closed. Sonnet P2.

- ✅ **Phase 25AZ — APPROACH A: POST-PARSEINP CLEANUP → RCLVARSYM = 5.0 (MAJOR MILESTONE, P1)**: Built `probe-phase25az-rclvar-ops-fix.mjs` with 2 approaches. **Approach A PASS**: After ParseInp("2+3") returns OP1=5.0 (903 steps), saved OP1, reset OPS→OPBase (0xD3FFF6) and FPS→FPSbase (0xD1A88A), re-ran CreateReal("Ans") at 0x08227C → new Ans data slot at DE=0xD1A88A, wrote saved [00 80 50 00 00 00 00 00 00] into slot, then RclVarSym at 0x09AC77 → OP1=[00 80 50 00 00 00 00 00 00]=5.0, 43 steps. **First validated full ParseInp→store→recall round-trip.** Second CreateReal shifts pointers (OPBase 0xD3FFF6→0xD3FFED, tempMem 0xD1A88A→0xD1A893) — expected behavior. Hypothesis: FindSym scan range (progPtr→pTemp) doesn't bracket the entry correctly, or errNo=0x8D interferes. Sonnet P1.

All critical parser flags zero: ParsFlag=0x00, ParsFlag2=0x00 (numOP1=0), numMode=0x00 (Normal), fmtOverride=0x00, hookflags4=0x00 (parserHookActive=0), progExecuting=0x00, onFlags=0x00 (parseInput=0, statsValid=0), trigFlags=0x00 (radian=0), graphFlags2=0x00 (splitOverride=0). **ParseInp changes only IY+0x07 (0xD00087) from 0x00→0x01** — no watched parser flag bytes change during ParseInp execution. **Our zero-state probes are fully validated**: the MEM_INIT baseline matches our probe assumptions exactly. fmtFlags bit 4 is MEM_INIT-set (not a probe artifact) but does not affect ParseInp("2+3") behavior. Sonnet P2.

### Completed (session 110)
- ✅ **Phase 25AY — OPS OVERFLOW = VAT ENTRY CORRUPTION ROOT CAUSE (MAJOR DISCOVERY, P1)**: Built `probe-phase25ay-rclvar-vat-dump.mjs` with 4 scenarios. **Scenario A** (control: CreateReal("A")+42.0 → RclVarSym): PASS, recalled 42.0 correctly. **Scenario B** (full pipeline: MEM_INIT→CreateReal("Ans")→ParseInp→RclVarSym): FAIL, OP1=9.1e-18 (garbage). VAT dump reveals: BEFORE ParseInp, VAT at 0xD3FFF8=[00 72 d1 a8 81 00 00 00] (valid Ans entry). AFTER ParseInp, VAT at 0xD3FFF8=[70 00 8a 9a 09 fe ff 7f] (corrupted). **The garbage OP1 is literally the corrupted VAT bytes.** Mechanism: OPS grows from 0xD3FFF6 to 0xD40002 during ParseInp (12 bytes upward), directly overwriting the VAT entry at 0xD3FFF8. **Scenario C** (higher userMem base 0xD1A8C0): FAIL, same garbage — FPS overlap is NOT the cause. **Scenario D** (FPS/OPS restoration after ParseInp): FAIL, same garbage — VAT entry is already corrupted before RclVarSym runs. Ans DATA at 0xD1A881 is intact (contains 5.0 BCD), but the VAT METADATA is destroyed. Sonnet P1.

Sonnet P2.

Following functions (0x09923A "MinToEdit", 0x09927F, 0x0992A0) form edit-buffer recall helpers. Session 98's "DisarmScroll" name was correct. Sonnet P3.

- ✅ **Phase 25AW — TRAMPOLINE INVESTIGATION COMPLETE (KEY SYNTHESIS)**: Sessions 99-108 fully characterized the trampoline path (0x0586E3→0x099910→0x07FF81→ParseInp). Root cause of trampoline failure: accidental error frame stack alignment. The trampoline's extra CALL shifts all stack positions by 3 bytes, moving 0x099929 from the HL (catch address) position to the AF (flags) position in JError's 18-byte frame pop. Fix: errSP must be set to ParseInp_SP - 6 (dynamic, not fixed). But the trampoline adds nothing for expression evaluation — 0x07FF81's List pre-seed is overwritten by ParseInp (session 100). **Direct ParseInp at 0x099914 with OP1=zeros is the correct and fully working approach.** Close the trampoline investigation; focus on full ENTER-handler simulation with direct ParseInp.

- ✅ **Phase 25AU — ERROR FRAME CLOBBERING MECHANISM IDENTIFIED (SECONDARY FINDING)**: The error frame at errSP=0xD1A86F is clobbered by TWO CALLs: (1) CALL 0x099910 at 0x0586E3 writes return address 0x0586E6 at 0xD1A872-0xD1A874 (overwrites ERR_CATCH_ADDR bytes), (2) CALL 0x07FF81 at 0x099910 writes return address 0x099914 at 0xD1A86F-0xD1A871 (overwrites first 3 frame bytes). For any entry via 0x0586E3, the error frame must be placed below the lowest SP reached during the CALL chain (0xD1A86C after 0x04C940 internal call), i.e., at ≤ 0xD1A866.

But POP AF at 0x05862F was NEVER reached — the early call chain (0x07FF7B at step 44, 0x08384F at step 50) runs before the NZ/Z branch and triggers RAM CLEAR → HALT loop at 0x006202 (197,932 of 200K hits). The NZ path requires far more OS state than just allocator pointers. **Implication: the bypass approach (entering at 0x0586CE) is definitively the correct strategy.**

FindSym at 0x083865 reads pTemp from 0xD0259A and progPtr from 0xD0259D for its VAT scan loop exit condition (`SBC HL,DE` where DE=pTemp+1). Correcting these addresses fixed the FindSym infinite loop.

When 0x058C65's RET executes, it pops the return address of whoever CALLed 0x0585E9 (CoorMon), not the instruction after the JP. The common tail at 0x058693 is only reachable via: (a) NZ path at 0x058630 `JR NZ 0x05866A` → allocator calls → falls through to 0x058693, or (b) history-recall path (numLastEntries>0) at 0x05863B-0x058668 → `JR 0x058693`. Empty-ENTER (numLastEntries=0) is a ParseInp dead end. Sonnet P3. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ar-post-empty-enter-disasm.mjs`, `phase25ar-post-empty-enter-disasm-report.md`.

- ✅ **Phase 25AR — FINDSYM LOOP AT 0x083865 FULLY DISASSEMBLED**: Loop exit condition: `SBC HL,DE; JR C, 0x0838C8` where HL=progPtr (walk position) and DE=pTemp+1 (boundary). Loop scans VAT entries backward from progPtr, reading type bytes (AND 0x3F), comparing variable names against OP1 (0xD005F8). Exit at 0x0838C8 = `POP DE; RET` (symbol not found). With pTemp=progPtr=0xD3FFFF (seeded correctly), the first iteration has HL=0xD3FFF8 < DE=0xD40000 → carry → immediate exit. Utility at 0x04C91C = zero-extend BC to 24 bits via scrapMem (0xD02AD7). ### Completed (session 102)
- ✅ **Phase 25AQ — VAT WALKER LOOP EXIT CONDITION FOUND (KEY FINDING)**: Static disassembly of 0x082745-0x0827CA. Loop structure: reads 3-byte VAT entry pointer via LD C,(HL)/DEC HL/LD B,(HL)/DEC HL/LD A,(HL), stores to scrapMem via CALL 0x04C876, calls 0x0821B2 (range check), optionally adjusts pointer, advances by entry size, then: `POP AF / OR A / SBC HL,BC / LD BC,(0xD02590) / SBC HL,BC / RET C`. **OPBase at 0xD02590 is the sole exit condition.** When HL (current walk position) drops below OPBase, the loop returns. With OPBase=0 (uninitialized), the comparison HL < 0 is unreachable in 24-bit unsigned arithmetic → infinite loop. Also found: 0xD02577 is loaded during the loop (unknown allocator boundary), 0x04C876 is just a scrapMem store (not a compare), sub at 0x08279E reads entry type byte (AND 0x3F) for variable-type dispatch. Per-pointer adjuster at 0x0827CA-0x082830 adjusts 11 system pointers if they fall within affected range. Sonnet P1. Artifacts: `probe-phase25aq-vat-walker-disasm.mjs`, `phase25aq-vat-walker-disasm-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25AQ — HISTORY BUFFER SEED TESTED (CONFIRMS ALLOCATOR AS SOLE BLOCKER)**: Seeded minimal history entry: 2-byte LE size (0x0004) at 0xD0150B, 4 bytes token data "2+3\n" at 0xD0150D, end pointer 0xD01511 at 0xD01508. Set numLastEntries=1 at 0xD01D0B. ENTER handler at 0x0585E9 ran 100K steps. History manager at 0x0921CB reached at step 58, consumed the entry correctly (numLastEntries 1→0). But execution fell into allocator loop at 0x082754 instead of reaching 0x058693 (common tail). The allocator loop is the same OPBase=0 issue. **Implication**: once OPBase is seeded correctly, BOTH the empty-ENTER and history-recall paths should terminate and reach ParseInp. Also confirmed: the LDIR computation at 0x0922A2 is `BC = (0xD01508) - entryAddr`, confirming session 101's wraparound analysis. Sub-function 0x092FDD walks the buffer with `LD HL,0xD0150B; DEC A; RET Z` loop. Sonnet P2. Artifacts: `probe-phase25aq-history-seed.mjs`, `phase25aq-history-seed-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25AQ — STAT-VAR EXHAUSTIVE 21/21 COMPLETE**: All 12 remaining tokens (tMinY=0x29, tMaxY=0x2A, tSigmaY=0x2B, tSigmaXY=0x2C, tr=0x2D, te=0x2E, ta=0x2F, tb=0x30, tc=0x31, td=0x32, tSSX=0x33, tSSY=0x34) PASS via Rcl_StatVar impl at 0x08019F. Each returns OP1=42.0 exact from seeded stat-var table. Combined with session 75's 9 validated tokens (0x20-0x28), all 21 one-variable stat tokens confirmed. Slot formula `addr = 0xD0117F + (token × 9)` proven for full range. Note: JT slot 0x0204F0 doesn't work for probes (transpiler hasn't lifted the JP dispatcher at that address) — must call impl 0x08019F directly. Sonnet P3 (fixed from initial FAIL). ### Completed (session 101)
- ✅ **Phase 25AP — ALLOCATOR LOOP CALL CHAIN FULLY TRACED (KEY FINDING)**: Empty-ENTER handler at 0x058C65 does NOT just do housekeeping and RET. At step 82 it enters sub 0x058C83→0x058CFF→0x058D2E. This path calls 0x07FF91 (Matrix type pre-seeder), FindSym(0x0846EA), PushErrorHandler(0x061DEF), then InsertMem(0x082438→0x08241A→0x0822D1 allocator core). The tight loop at 0x082745-0x0827AA starts by step 464, walking a linked list/block table via 0x04C876 (compare helper). With RAM uninitialized after MEM_INIT, the list has no terminator → infinite iteration. SP drops from 0xD1A86C (entry) to 0xD1A842 (allocator, 14 levels deep). **Root cause**: VAT/free-space chain needs a proper terminator. The outer loop at 0x058C87 re-enters the allocator after each InsertMem return, compounding the problem. Sonnet P1. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ap-allocator-after-enter.mjs`, `phase25ap-allocator-after-enter-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25AP — 0xFFF909 = CORRUPTED ADDRESS, NOT VALID ROM (CLOSED)**: 0xFFF909 is 0xBFF909 bytes past ROM end (0x3FFFFF) — in unmapped RAM space. When numLastEntries=1 but history buffer at 0xD0150B is all zeros, 0x0922A2 computes BC=mem[0xD01508]-entryAddr but 0xD01508=0x000000. Subtraction wraps to ~3M → LDIR at 0x0922AE copies ~3M bytes through entire 16MB address space → stack corrupted → RET pops 0xFFF909 as return address. History buffer format: 2-byte size prefix at entry address, followed by token data, end pointer at 0xD01508. To test history-recall path, must seed valid entry — NOT a transpiler seed issue. Probe ran 42 steps confirming the exact corruption mechanism. Sonnet P2. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ap-fff909-check.mjs`, `probe-phase25ap-disasm-092297.mjs`, `phase25ap-fff909-check-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25AP — 0x07FF81 = LIST-TYPE PRE-SEEDER, MULTI-ENTRY PATTERN (RESOLVED)**: 0x07FF81 is one of ~8 entry points (0x07FF81-0x07FFBF) that converge at 0x07FF87→0x07FF99→0x04C940 to store a type byte + name/index into OP1 and scrapMem(0xD02AD7). Entry 0x07FF81: type=0x05 (List), index=0x23. 0x04C940 stores HL to scrapMem, zeros high byte (0xD02AD9), reloads HL — a round-trip store. 0xD02AD7 = `scrapMem` per ti84pceg.inc ("3 byte scrap (unstable)"), 108 ROM references. 3 callers of 0x07FF81: trampoline 0x099910 (ENTER path at 0x0586E3), 0x058641 (home-screen dispatch), 0x08384B. 12 callers go directly to ParseInp at 0x099914, skipping pre-seed. 0x07FF8D (Matrix, A=0x03) is most popular with 31 callers. The pre-seed is a default variable context for bare variable references; expression evaluation ("2+3") overwrites it completely. Sonnet P3. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ap-trampoline-preseed.mjs`, `phase25ap-trampoline-preseed-report.md`.

- ✅ **Phase 25AO — Z-FLAG CORRECTION: POP AF ALREADY RESTORES Z (CORRECTS session 99)**: PUSH AF at 0x058621 saves flags from CALL 0x058212 at 0x05861D. 0x058212 calls 0x0800B8 which does `BIT 5,(IY+0x44)` [addr 0xD000C4]. Four scenarios tested: (A) baseline = Z path taken, empty-ENTER hit at step 75, then allocator loop; (B) force bit5=0 = identical (already 0); (C) D01D0B=1 = missing_block at 0xFFF909 after 99 steps; (D) both = same as C. Scenario B (trampoline 0x099910) = 921 steps, OP1=5.0, errNo=0x8D, 0x07FF81 visited. Identical outputs, +3 steps for the trampoline call. Handler is self-contained: calls 0x0800A8 (guard, RET NZ at 0x058C69), calls sub at 0x058C83 (which calls 0x07FF7B, 0x08384F, CloseEditEqu, flag manipulation), then SET 5,(IY+12), RES 4,(IY+5), RES 1,(IY+69), RET at 0x058C82. Has 10 RET instructions and ZERO jumps/falls-through to 0x058693 (the common tail where ParseInp is called at 0x0586E3). Sub at 0x058C83 includes error-guarded allocation of a 100-byte type-0x2E variable via PushErrorHandler. The only JP is JP Z,0x061D42 (error handler). **Implication**: on fresh boot with no expression typed, ENTER correctly skips ParseInp. ParseInp is only invoked when (a) the NZ path succeeds (has existing expression in edit buffer) or (b) nonzero numLastEntries recalls last entry → both converge at 0x058693. Sonnet P3. Depth 5 via home-handler root: 0x0A6295. 0x057921 is NOT the second-pass target — it lives inside a function-pointer dispatch table at 0x0578FA for a non-home app context. 0x020F00 = JT slot 895 (JP, not CALL). Static probe only.

### Completed (session 93)
- ✅ **Phase 25AH — 0x04C990 = negate-BC utility, NOT cxCurApp zeroing (CORRECTS session 92)** — Full disassembly of 0x04C950-0x04CA50 (256 bytes). 0x04C990 is a 12-byte function: `push hl; ld hl,0; or a; sbc hl,bc; push hl; pop bc; pop hl; ret`. Zero memory writes — only stack PUSH/POP. The entire region is a library of arithmetic helpers: 0x04C950=divHL_by_10, 0x04C963=divHL_by_A_24bit, 0x04C973=cpHL_DE_preserve, 0x04C979=cpHL_DE_24bit, 0x04C980=min_HL_BC, 0x04C990=negate_BC, 0x04C99C=negate_DE, 0x04C9A8=signExtTemp_store. None reference cxCurApp (0xD007E0) or cxMain (0xD007CA). Session 92's watchpoint reporting PC=0x04C990 was misattributed — likely post-write PC advancement where the actual zeroing instruction was 1-2 steps earlier in the caller's instruction stream. Sonnet P1 created probe + ran and verified by Opus. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ah-disasm-04C990.mjs`, `phase25ah-disasm-04C990-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25AH — Home-screen handler TWO-PASS DISPATCH MODEL (KEY DISCOVERY)** — Runtime trace of 0x058241 directly (bypassing CoorMon) with full OS state seeding (MEM_INIT, cxMain=0x058241, cxCurApp=0x40, ENTER key, tokenized "2+3"). Ran 50,000 steps, collected 418 unique PCs. **ParseInp (0x099914) NOT reached.** None of the 9 monitored entry points (ParseInp, CreateReal, RclVarSym, ChkFindSym, FPAdd, JError, GetCSC, PutC, PutMap) were hit. Handler processes ~92 steps (checking IY flags, scan codes, app state), then calls 0x08BF22 at step 95. 0x08BF22 chains: 0x042366→0x0421A7→0x000310→0x001C55→0x001C33 (known ISR dispatch infinite loop). **This confirms a two-pass dispatch model**: ENTER handler sets state/flags and yields back to event loop; CoorMon re-dispatches to ParseInp on a subsequent iteration. 0x08BF22 = "yield to event loop" mechanism. Sonnet P2 created probe + ran and verified by Opus. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ah-homehandler-trace.mjs`, `phase25ah-homehandler-trace-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25AH — Browser-shell direct ParseInp bypass ADDED** — Modified browser-shell.html with a "Direct Eval (ParseInp bypass)" section: text input field + Eval/Clear buttons + result display. Pipeline mirrors the validated session 92 probe exactly: cold boot → kernel init → post-init → MEM_INIT → write tokens to userMem → clear OP1 → seed error frame → run ParseInp → decode BCD result → reset FPS/OPS. Token support: digits 0-9, +, -, *, /, (, ), decimal point, unary negation (0xB0 vs 0x71). Each eval runs in its own fresh memory/executor instance. Existing boot sequence and home-screen render completely unaffected. Sonnet P3 created integration + verified by Opus (probe-level only — browser testing deferred to next session). Artifacts: modified `browser-shell.html`.

All 24 bytes of cx range (0xD007CA-0xD007E1) zeroed in a single burst. PC 0x001881 = `LD HL,0xD00000; LD DE,0xD00001; LD BC,0x013FD7; LD (HL),0; LDIR` — zeroes 81,879 bytes of ALL OS RAM (0xD00000-0xD13FD7). CoorMon falls through to this cold-restart because cxMain and handler pointers are all zeros (no valid dispatch targets). **Implication**: must seed full cx context (not just cxCurApp) via NewContext or manual bulk copy before CoorMon can dispatch. - ✅ **Phase 25AF — Store+recall with correct tokens: INFORMATIVE FAIL (pipeline design issue)** — Fixed tokens [0x32,0x70,0x33,0x3F] didn't change behavior: ParseInp still 253 steps, OP1=0, errNo=0x00. Root cause: creating Ans BEFORE ParseInp causes token-stream-redirect — OP1=zeros maps to Ans, ParseInp finds it via ChkFindSym and redirects token stream to Ans data area (all zeros). begPC shifted to 0xD1A883 (DE+2 of Ans slot). The token encoding was never the issue; the probe pipeline design is wrong. Fix: don't create Ans before ParseInp — let StoAns auto-create during expression evaluation. Session 87's hypothesis "for reading error strings" was WRONG — flash unlock provides privileged mode for IY flag writes. Error strings ("OVERFLOW", "DOMAIN", "SYNTAX", "UNDEFINED", "MEMORY", "BREAK") at 0x062300-0x0628FF in flash, accessed during DispErrorScreen, not JError. **For transpilation**: flash unlock call is a no-op; preserve errNo store + IY flag bits + SP restore. ### Completed (session 88)
- ✅ **Phase 25AC — ParseInp "variable recall" = TOKEN STREAM REDIRECT (ROOT CAUSE)** — P1 probe dumped memory around DE before/after ParseInp with OP1=varA + stored 42.0. begPC was set to 0xD1A883 (DE+2), curPC to 0xD1A884 — ParseInp redirected the token stream to the variable's data area, parsing BCD bytes as tokens. With overlapping 42.0 writes (probe design flaw), got errNo=0x88 and missing_block at 273 steps. BUT the key finding stands: stored 42.0 at DE was NOT overwritten by ParseInp in the clean P2 probe (variable A data survived intact at `[00 81 42 00 00 00 00 00 00]`). The "recall returns 0.0" mystery is solved: ParseInp doesn't recall — it re-parses variable content as tokens. For Real variables (9 BCD bytes, not token data), this produces 0.0. Sonnet P1 created probe + ran. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ac-recall-offset.mjs`, `phase25ac-recall-offset-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25AC — Both vars (A+Ans) confirms errNo is OP1-content-driven** — Scenario A (both vars, OP1=varA): 720 steps, errNo=0x00, OP1=0.0 (same "found" path). Scenario B (both vars, OP1=zeros): 908 steps, errNo=0x8D, OP1=5.0 (Ans existence reduces steps by 11). Scenario C (control): 919 steps. Creating Ans does NOT clear errNo=0x8D; only having OP1 point to a valid variable name clears it. Variable "A" data (42.0) survived ParseInp in Scenario A — confirming ParseInp doesn't modify variable data during the "found" path. Sonnet P2 created probe + ran and verified. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ac-both-vars.mjs`, `phase25ac-both-vars-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25AC — StoAns STORES 5.0 when Ans exists (CONFIRMED)** — Full PC trace comparison: Without Ans (919 steps), StoAns sets OP1[0]=0xFF at step 870 (PC=0x099A9B), ChkFindSym at step 879, FindSym at step 890, both fail → 49-step failure path (PCs 0x099ABA/0x099ABF/0x099AC1). With Ans pre-created (903 steps), StoAns at step 875 jumps from 0x099AB3 directly to 0x099AF1 (skipping ChkFindSym entirely), OP1[0] NEVER reaches 0xFF, and FindSym success path uses PCs 0x084711/0x08471B/0x084723. **Ans data at DE=0xD1A881 contains `[00 80 50 00 00 00 00 00 00]` = 5.0 after ParseInp.** The 16-step difference is exactly the failed ChkFindSym path being eliminated. errNo=0x8D persists in both scenarios (set at step 27/32 by initial ChkFindSym on OP1=zeros). Sonnet P3 created probe + ran and verified. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ac-stoans-trace.mjs`, `phase25ac-stoans-trace-report.md`.

Sonnet P3 created probe + ran and verified. Artifacts: `probe-phase25ab-error-routine-disasm.mjs`, `phase25ab-error-routine-disasm-report.md`.

### Completed (session 85)
- ✅ **Phase 25Z — PopErrorHandler seed ADDED (0x061DD1)** — Only this address was missing from transpiled blocks; 0x061DB2 (JError), 0x061DEF (PushErrorHandler), and 0x061E27 (normal-return stub) already existed as transpiled blocks. Added all 4 as explicit seeds in `scripts/transpile-ti84-rom.mjs`. Retranspiled: 143,548 blocks (+1 new), 699,726 covered bytes (+29). PopErrorHandler (0x061DD1-0x061DEE) is a 30-byte stub: `LD HL,(OPBase); POP DE (opsDelta); ADD HL,DE; LD (OPS),HL; POP DE (fpsDelta); LD HL,(FPSbase); ADD HL,DE; LD (FPS),HL; POP HL (prevErrSP); LD (errSP),HL; LD A,(errNo); RET`. Codex P1 added seeds; Opus retranspiled and verified. Artifacts: modified `scripts/transpile-ti84-rom.mjs`.
- ✅ **Phase 25Z — Full error-frame probe CHANGED BEHAVIOR** — With PopErrorHandler now transpiled, the 25Y probe no longer fails at 37 steps with missing_block. Now runs 50K steps (max_steps), errorRestoreHits=1 (PopErrorHandler fires), but all allocator pointers zeroed and stuck at 0x006202. **ROOT CAUSE**: probe's hlPayload=0x000000 becomes PopErrorHandler's RET address → execution jumps to 0x000000 (boot entry) → reinitializes everything → counting loop. The full error frame needs ParseInp's actual error continuation address as hlPayload, which is unknown. The minimal 6-byte catch frame (25X probe) works because longjmp bypasses PopErrorHandler entirely. Artifacts: probe results only (no new files).
- ✅ **Phase 25Z — CreateReal + ParseInp FULL PIPELINE (MAJOR FINDING)** — MEM_INIT (18 steps) → CreateReal("A") at 0x08238A (231 steps, errNo=0x00, OPBase 0xD3FFFF→0xD3FFF6 delta=-9, DE=0xD1A881 points to 9 zero bytes of new variable) → ParseInp (253 steps, errNo=0x00). **errNo=0x8D IS FIXED by pre-creating variable "A"**. BUT OP1=[00 41 00 00 00 00 00 00 00] (unchanged from variable name setup), decoded=0, NOT 5.0. Parser with pre-created variable follows a DIFFERENT code path — returns in 253 steps (vs 918 without variable) without computing the expression. **Hypothesis**: ParseInp's ChkFindSym at entry finds variable "A" in VAT → parser takes "recall variable" path instead of "parse expression" path. Variable data at DE=0xD1A881 is all zeros post-ParseInp (5.0 not stored there either). Codex P3 created probe; Sonnet P3 ran and verified. Artifacts: `probe-phase25z-full-pipeline.mjs`, `phase25z-full-pipeline-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25Z — Executor fallback investigation COMPLETE** — Confirmed executor has NO raw-byte interpreter fallback (cpu-runtime.js:1064-1087). When a PC has no transpiled block, it tries skipping up to 16 bytes ahead; if no block found, terminates with 'missing_block'. ParseInp's 918-step run visits only 3 error-region PCs (0x061D3A, 0x061DB2, 0x061DBA), all transpiled blocks — zero missing-block events. PopErrorHandler (0x061DD1) is never visited in the minimal catch frame path because longjmp does `LD SP,(errSP); POP AF; RET` directly to FAKE_RET. Normal-return cleanup stub at 0x061E27 decoded: 3× POP AF (discard error frame entries), EX (SP),HL + LD (errSP),HL (restore previous errSP), cleanup, RET. Codex P2 created probe+report; Sonnet P2 also created versions and ran probe. Artifacts: `probe-phase25z-executor-fallback.mjs`, `phase25z-executor-fallback-report.md`.
- Golden regression 26/26 PASS post-session (verified twice). Codex: 3/3 completed (P1 seeds, P2 probe+report, P3 probe+report). Sonnet fallback: 2/2 completed (P2 investigation, P3 pipeline probe — both ran independently since Codex took long).

### Completed (session 84)
- ✅ **Phase 25Y — ParseInp OP1=5.0 CONFIRMED as current behavior (NOT a Sonnet-only result)** — Ran committed probe `probe-phase25x-meminit-then-parseinp.mjs` and verified: 918 steps, OP1=[00 80 50 00 00 00 00 00 00]=5.0, errNo=0x8D, curPC=0xD00804 (past endPC). Free space 153,470 bytes. FPS moved -9 (one var allocated), OPS moved +3. The "500K steps stuck at 0x006202" described in session 83 priorities was pre-OPS-fix behavior and NO LONGER REPRODUCES. Opus verified independently.
- ❌ **Phase 25Y — Full PushErrorHandler frame probe FAILS at 37 steps** — Built proper 18-byte frame with [0x061E27, 0x061DD1, OPS-OPBase, FPS-FPSbase, prevErrSP, hlPayload]. All 3 token terminator variants (0x3F/0x04/0x00) hit missing block at 0x061DD1 after only 37 steps. OP1=0, curPC unchanged. **ROOT CAUSE**: JError/PushErrorHandler addresses 0x061DB2-0x061E27 are NOT in transpiled blocks. The executor's raw-byte fallback apparently handles these blocks in the committed probe (918 steps), but direct entry via the full error frame triggers a hard missing-block stop. Adding these addresses as transpiler seeds is the fix. Codex P1 created probe; Sonnet P1 confirmed results. Artifacts: `probe-phase25y-parseinp-full-errframe.mjs`, `phase25y-parseinp-full-errframe-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25Y — ParseInp entry FULLY DISASSEMBLED (KEY FINDINGS)** — Static decode of 0x099914..0x099954 + helpers 0x099B81/0x099B18/0x09BEED. Entry: `XOR A; LD (0xD022BE),A` (clear flag), calls 0x099B81 twice (clears 12 IY flag bits: IY+6,7=0, res bits in IY+20,26,31,32,48,49,62,72,73,88). Then `CALL 0x099B18` which calls ChkFindSym, and if found: walks VAT entry (skip 9 bytes + var size + 1), stores to asm_data_ptr2 (0xD00687), calls helpers, WRITES begPC and curPC: `LD (0xD02317),HL; LD (0xD0231A),HL`. **ParseInp writes curPC from VAT data, does NOT read caller-seeded value.** Token reading confirmed deeper at 0x09BAB8: `LD BC,(curPC); LD HL,(endPC); SBC HL,BC; LD A,(HL)` — reads byte at curPC, checks bounds. OPS (0xD02593) is read by helper 0x09BEED after allocation via 0x082BB5 — it's a downward-growing OPS stack for parser operands, NOT a token reader. Codex P2 + Sonnet P2 both produced results. Artifacts: `probe-phase25y-parseinp-entry-disasm.mjs`, `phase25y-parseinp-entry-disasm-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25Y — 0x006202 diagnosis: valid ROM code, not garbage** — ROM bytes: `B7 ED 52 20 FB 3D 20 E5` = `OR A; SBC HL,DE; JR NZ,-5; DEC A; JR NZ,...` — a counting/multiplication loop. Only reached in pre-OPS-fix probes where corrupted error recovery left HL≠DE. Current probe never visits this address. Codex P3 + Sonnet P3 confirmed. Artifacts: `probe-phase25y-006202-diagnosis.mjs`, `phase25y-006202-diagnosis-report.md`.
- Golden regression 26/26 PASS post-session. Codex: 3/3 completed (P1 did all tasks in one run, P2 disasm + report, P3 diagnosis + report). Sonnet: 3/3 completed (P1 confirmed full-frame failure, P2 found curPC reader at 0x09BAB8, P3 confirmed 0x006202 not reproducible).

### Completed (session 83)
- ✅ **Phase 25X — ErrMemory ROOT CAUSE FOUND AND FIXED (BREAKTHROUGH)** — Free-space check at 0x0820b5 computes `OPS(0xD02593) - FPS(0xD0258D)`. All prior ParseInp probes (sessions 73-82) set OPS to the token buffer address (0xD00800 or 0xD1A881), placing it BELOW FPS → zero free space → ErrMemory. **Fix**: leave OPS at MEM_INIT default (0xD3FFFF), address tokens through begPC/curPC/endPC (0xD02317/1A/1D). The complete error path: 0x082bb5 CALL 0x082266 (space check wrapper) → 0x08226b CALL 0x0820b5 (free calc: `LD HL,(OPS); LD BC,(FPS); SBC HL,BC`) → if negative: LD HL,0 → RET → SBC HL,DE (free-required) → carry set → GC attempt at 0x082273 (pTemp-OPBase check) → still fails → RET carry → 0x082bb9 RET NC (not taken) → 0x082bba JP 0x061d3e (ErrMemory). Opus decoded all 4 code regions independently before Codex/Sonnet ran. Artifacts: `probe-phase25x-error-path-disasm.mjs`, `phase25x-error-path-disasm-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25X — MEM_INIT then ParseInp — NO MORE ErrMemory (MAJOR PROGRESS)** — Added 0x09DEE0 and 0x08A98F as transpiler seeds (already reachable via CFG — block/coverage counts unchanged at 143,547/699,697). Called MEM_INIT at 0x09DEE0: completed in 17 steps. Post-MEM_INIT state: tempMem/FPSbase/FPS=0xD1A881, OPBase/OPS/pTemp/progPtr=0xD3FFFF, newDataPtr=0xD1A881, flashSize=0x0C0000. Then ParseInp with tokens at 0xD00800 via begPC/curPC/endPC, OPS left at 0xD3FFFF: **500,000 steps, errNo=0x00, NO ErrMemory!** Parser enters ChkFindSym(0x08383d)→FindSym(0x0846ea) at step 17, then runs for 500K steps and gets stuck at PC=0x006202 (real ROM code, byte=0xB7). All allocator pointers zeroed after run (suspicious). **First ParseInp run that passes the free-space check.** Codex P3 created probe; Opus ran and verified. Artifacts: `probe-phase25x-meminit-then-parseinp.mjs`, seeds in `scripts/transpile-ti84-rom.mjs`.
- ✅ **Phase 25X — 0x08A98F = graph-window initializer (NOT memory-related)** — Full disassembly: `LD HL, 0x08A97B; JR +4; LD DE, 0xD014FC (YOffset); JP 0x07F976 (Mov10B)`. Copies 10 bytes of graph-window defaults from ROM to RAM 0xD014FC..0xD01505. Alternate entry at 0x08A995 loads source from 0x08A971. 0x07F976 = 10× LDI + RET. **This routine does NOT affect ParseInp's memory allocation** — it initializes graph parameters (YMin, YMax, etc.). The remaining MEM_INIT actions post-pointers (IY+71 bit 7, flash size computation) are the only potentially relevant setup, and the probe shows MEM_INIT handles them in just 17 steps. Codex P1 created probe+report; Sonnet P1 also created versions. Artifacts: `probe-phase25x-08a98f-disasm.mjs`, `phase25x-08a98f-disasm-report.md`.

- ✅ **Phase 25W — MEM_INIT FULLY DISASSEMBLED (KEY DISCOVERY)** — Entry at 0x09DEE0, preceded by RET at 0x09DEDF. Full disassembly: `LD HL, 0xD1A881` → writes tempMem(0xD02587), FPSbase(0xD0258A), FPS(0xD0258D), newDataPtr(0xD025A0) all to userMem. Then `LD HL, 0xD3FFFF` → writes pTemp(0xD0259A), OPBase(0xD02590), OPS(0xD02593), progPtr(0xD0259D) all to symTable end. Continues: CALL 0x08A98F, SET 7,(IY+71), then flash-size computation (CALL 0x000600, arithmetic, CALL 0x04C9EA, writes 0xD025C5) ending with RET at 0x09DF34. Each primary is seeded from chkDelPtr3 (0xD02581), secondary from asm_ram (0xD00687), then pointed byte cleared to 0x00. Slot A (0xD01FEA) has 8 ROM refs (5 READ, 2 WRITE, 1 LITERAL), reads go through CALL 0x04C973 (compare helper). Secondary companions at +3 offset: 0xD01FED=26 refs, 0xD01FF3=10 refs, 0xD01FF9=49 refs — much more heavily used. The surrounding gap 0xD01FC0..0xD0203C has 19 distinct referenced RAM addresses with 159 total ROM hits. Strong co-location with editSym/editDat references. - ✅ **Phase 25V — VAT/heap initializer FOUND at 0x09DEE9 (KEY DISCOVERY)** — Static ROM scan found ALL references to OPBase/OPS/pTemp/progPtr/FPSbase/FPS. **243 total refs, 56 writes, 11 clusters**. The REAL initializer is **Cluster 11 at 0x09DEE9..0x09DF05**: 6 consecutive `LD (nn), HL` stores writing FPSbase→FPS→(newDataPtr 0xD025A0)→pTemp→OPBase→OPS→progPtr. The routine at 0x09DEF5 loads `LD HL, 0xD3FFFF` (symTable end) before writing pTemp/OPBase/OPS/progPtr. **Initial values are 0xD3FFFF (symTable), NOT 0xD1A881 (userMem)** — this explains why our probes with OPBase=userMem hit ErrMemory. Other notable clusters: 0x0820FA (4 ptrs, likely allocator cleanup), 0x083675 (4 ptrs, likely memory compaction), 0x09DCAF (2 ptrs, secondary init). Codex created probe; Opus ran and verified. ROM refs concentrated in graph/finance code: 0x04xxxx (finance routines), 0x0Axxxx (graph renderer), 0x06xxxx (graphing engine), 0x0Bxxxx (program editor). All 3 are loaded as addresses into HL/DE for InsertMem adjustment — they're pointers INTO graph/finance data, not the data itself. Codex created probe; Opus ran and verified. - ✅ **Phase 25U — signExtTemp pipeline FULLY DOCUMENTED** — Static disassembly of the complete InsertMem pointer-adjustment pipeline: (1) 0x04C9A8 = signExtTemp scratch helper: stores HL to 0xD02AD7, performs 24-bit arithmetic right shift (SRL A → RR H → RR L), rewrites via SIS prefix, reloads HL and returns. (2) 0x082823 = per-pointer adjuster: reads 3-byte ptr from (HL), compares against DE via SBC. `ret nc` skips if ptr >= DE. On carry path: loads delta from signExtTemp into BC, loads ptr into IX, adds delta, writes back. (3) 0x0827CA = calling loop: stores BC directly to signExtTemp, then iterates over **11 system pointer slots** (pTemp, progPtr, editSym, tSymPtr1/2, chkDelPtr3/4, plus 4 newly-discovered slots: 0xD01FEA, 0xD01FF0, 0xD01FF6, 0xD02567) calling adjustOnePtr for each. Pipeline: `InsertMem(BC)→negate(BC)→store(signExtTemp)→adjust(11 slots)`. Codex succeeded on first attempt + Sonnet verified. Artifacts: `probe-phase25u-signexttemp.mjs`, `phase25u-signexttemp-report.md`.

Added post-allocation state dump: DE=0x7FFFFF (sentinel area), OP1 zeroed by allocator, OPBase corrupted 0xD1A881→0xA88100, pTemp/progPtr zeroed, heap top=0xFFFFF7 (= 0 + (-9) = 0xFFFFF7), VAT area empty, errNo=0x00. - ✅ **Phase 25T — 0x04C990 = BC-NEGATE HELPER (NOT pointer adjuster)** — Static disassembly reveals just 12 bytes: `push hl; ld hl,0; or a; sbc hl,bc; push hl; pop bc; pop hl; ret`. Computes BC = -BC. Does NOT read or write any RAM pointers. Session 78's hypothesis that 0x04C990 adjusts OPBase/pTemp/progPtr was WRONG — it just prepares the negative delta for the actual pointer adjusters. Codex succeeded on first attempt. Artifacts: `probe-phase25t-ptr-adjuster.mjs`, `phase25t-ptr-adjuster-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25T — InsertMem pointer-update subs FULLY MAPPED** — All 4 InsertMem sub-calls disassembled + their call targets: (1) **0x082739** = VAT pointer walker: walks backward from 0xD3FFFF to OPBase, adjusting VAT entry data pointers in the moved range. Reads OPBase as loop bound only. (2) **0x0824D6** = edit-buffer adjuster: adjusts editCursor/editTail/editBtm at 0xD02317/1A/1D. (3) **0x0824FD** = bulk pointer updater: adjusts 12 pointer slots via 0x0825D1 primitive (0xD0066F-D00684, D0069F, D006A2, D0256A, D025A0). (4) **0x082823** = actual per-pointer adjuster: reads signExtTemp from 0xD02AD7, applies `if ptr >= DE: ptr += signExtTemp`. Called from 0x0827CA for pTemp, progPtr, and 5 other system pointers (0xD0244E, 0xD0257B-0xD02584). **KEY FINDING: OPBase (0xD02590) is NEVER WRITTEN by any InsertMem sub**. The corruption 0xD1A881→0xA88100 is from LDIR/LDDR block move physically overwriting OPBase's storage location because fake seed values put OPBase in the moved range. Codex P4 failed; Sonnet P2 and P4 both succeeded with comprehensive coverage. Artifacts: `probe-phase25t-insertmem-subs.mjs`, `phase25t-insertmem-subs-report.md`, `phase25t-ptr-adjuster-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25T — PushErrorHandler DISASSEMBLED + ParseInp PASS (MAJOR BREAKTHROUGH)** — PushErrorHandler at 0x061DEF pushes 18-byte ADL frame: (1) normal-return cleanup stub 0x061E27, (2) error-restore stub 0x061DD1, (3) OPS-OPBase delta, (4) FPS-FPSbase delta, (5) previous errSP, (6) caller's handler address. Longjmp at 0x061DB2 does `ld sp,(errSP); pop af; ret` → landing at PopErrorHandler 0x061DD1 which restores OPS/FPS/errSP. **ParseInp called with seeded errSP + FPSbase(0xD0258A)/FPS(0xD0258D) → RETURNS TO FAKE_RET after 85,312 steps.** errNo=0x8E (ErrMemory). Parser internally catches ErrUndefined at 0x061D3A → JError → recovery at 0x099929 → cleanup at 0x082266 → ErrMemory at 0x061D3E → JError → returns to FAKE_RET. OP1 unchanged ([00 41 00 00 00 00 00 00 00]). **First successful ParseInp return in project history.** Critical missing piece was FPSbase/FPS seeding — without valid FPS pointers the longjmp cleanup crashed. Codex P3 succeeded on first attempt. Artifacts: `probe-phase25t-parseinp-errhandler.mjs`, `phase25t-parseinp-errhandler-report.md`.

### Completed (session 78)
- ✅ **Phase 25S — Seed 0x0821A3 — CreateReal NOW COMPLETES** — Block 0x0821A3 is just `POP HL; RET` (2-byte allocator epilogue). Added as transpiler seed, retranspiled. CreateReal now runs through the full allocator path: 0x082159 loop (8 iter) → 0x07f7bd → 0x08012d → 0x082167-0x08219c → 0x04c990 → 0x0827c3 → VAT traversal (8 iter) → 0x0821a3 (POP HL; RET) → returns to sentinel 0xFFFFFF. errNo=0x00 (no error). OPBase still corrupted to 0xA88100 (expected with fake seed values). Sonnet fallback (Codex unavailable). Artifacts: modified `scripts/transpile-ti84-rom.mjs`, `phase25s-seed-0x0821a3-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25S — InsertMem 0x0821B9 DISASSEMBLED** — Core memory insertion routine: (1) grows heap top 0xD0258A by BC bytes, (2) grows VAT region 0xD0258D by BC, (3) block-copies data upward via unrolled LDDR (9 per iteration), (4) adjusts 0xD02587 directly by +BC, (5) handles VAT data at 0xD025A0 with secondary LDDR pass, (6) calls 4 pointer-update subroutines: **0x04C990** (system area — likely the centralized pointer adjuster), **0x082739**, **0x0824D6**, **0x0824FD**. **Critical insight**: OPBase (0xD02590), pTemp (0xD0259A), and progPtr (0xD0259D) are NOT directly adjusted by InsertMem — they must be updated by one of these sub-calls. Sonnet fallback. Artifacts: `probe-phase25s-subroutine-disasm.mjs`, `phase25s-subroutine-disasm-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25S — 0x082BBE region mapped** — Not a single subroutine but ~15 small utility functions: stream byte reader (reads from pointer at 0xD025A3, auto-advances), HL+6/HL-7 helpers for VAT entry navigation, 3-byte pointer read/write primitives, type classifier (AND 0x3F + table lookup), FindSym wrappers with 3 error-handling flavors (find-or-error, find-or-error+flag-reset, error-if-found for duplicate-create prevention). Error exits to 0x061D96, 0x061D92, 0x061D3A. Sonnet fallback. Artifacts: same as InsertMem above.
- ✅ **Phase 25S — errNo=0x88 = E_Syntax RESOLVED** — Error 0x88 = `8 + E_EDIT` (0x80) = Syntax Error with "allow re-edit" flag. 7 write sites to errNo in ROM: canonical ThrowError at 0x061DB2 plus save/clear/restore patterns in parser (e.g. 0x08515E-0x08516D saves errNo, clears it, calls variable lookup, unconditionally restores). VAT loop at 0x084711 is linear backward search comparing 3-byte name keys from OP1+1 (0xD005F9-FB). **Hypothesis confirmed**: longjmp fires but is caught by PushErrorHandler frame set up before ParseInp. errNo=0x88 persists as latent RAM state — normal TI-OS behavior, not a transpiler bug. Sonnet fallback. Artifacts: `probe-phase25s-errno88.mjs`, `phase25s-errno88-report.md`.
- ✅ **Phase 25S — Type guard 0x080084 DISASSEMBLED** — Three entry points: (1) 0x080084: tests raw A against 0x15 (equation), 0x17 (complex), falls through to 0x05 (real), 0x16 (new equation), 0x06 (list). (2) 0x08008C: loads A from OP1[0] via GetTypeFromOP1 (0x07F7BD = `LD A,(0xD005F8); AND 0x3F; RET`) then falls into same test chain. (3) 0x0800A0: CheckSplitFlag entry (IY+0x14 bit 3). Accepted type codes: **0x05** (real), **0x06** (list), **0x15** (equation), **0x16** (new equation), **0x17** (complex). Name-length helper 0x0820CD: CPIR scan of OP1[1..8] for null terminator, returns length in A (1-8). List vars (OP1[1]=0x5D) get length bumped to 2. A≥7 rejection by caller. Sonnet fallback. Artifacts: `probe-phase25s-typeguard-disasm.mjs`, `phase25s-typeguard-disasm-report.md`.
- Golden regression 26/26 PASS post-session. All 4 Codex dispatches failed (0-byte output); all 4 Sonnet fallbacks succeeded.

### Completed (session 77)
- ✅ **Phase 25R — Create allocator 0x0822D9 FULLY MAPPED** — Static disassembly of the shared Create allocator that CreateReal/CreateCplx/all CreateXxx variants jump to. **Full control flow**: (1) stores type byte A→OP1[0] at 0x0822D9, (2) calls 0x080084 type guard (Z flag determines path), (3) reads OP1+1 for name prefix — `]` (0x5D, list) takes special path via 0x0820CD (name-length helper) with A≥7 rejection→0x061D1A error, all other prefixes branch to 0x08234A alternate path, (4) saves computed A, calls 0x082BBE (pointer/slot helper, preserves HL→BC=size), (5) calls 0x0821B9 (heap/VAT move), (6) snapshots result pointer DE→OP1+3, clears OP1+2, restores count→OP1+6, computes BC=count+7, calls 0x0820F1, reloads DE from OP1+3, returns at 0x082349. **Subroutines**: 0x080084, 0x0820CD, 0x082BBE, 0x0821B9, 0x07F8A2, 0x0820F1. **Error exits**: `jp nc, 0x061D1A` and 0x082BB9→0x061D3E. **Reads-before-write**: OP1+1(0xD005F9), OP4(0xD00619). CreateTemp helper 0x08359B also mapped: increments pTempCnt(0xD02596), writes `$`→OP1+1, calls FindSym(0x0846EA). Artifacts: `probe-phase25r-create-allocator.mjs`, `phase25r-create-allocator-report.md`.
- ❌ **Phase 25R — CreateReal errSP — INFORMATIVE FAIL (MAJOR PROGRESS)** — errSP seeding technique worked correctly (frame at 0xD1A869, ERR_CATCH_ADDR=0x7FFFFA). But error handler NEVER FIRED — the allocator ran through its NORMAL path, not the error dispatch. PC trace: 0x082159 loop (8 iterations) → 0x07f7bd → 0x08012d → 0x082167-0x08219c → 0x04c990 → 0x0827c3 → 0x0827df-0x08282d (VAT traversal loop, 8 iterations) → 0x0821a3 → 0xFFFFFF (missing_block). **The failure is a missing transpiled block at 0x0821A3's successor**, not an error dispatch. errNo stayed 0x00. OPBase corrupted from 0xD1A881 to 0xA88100 (suggests pointer arithmetic went wrong with our seed values). VAT pointer seeds: OPBase=0xD1A881, pTemp=0xD1A88A, progPtr=0xD1A893 (probe auto-seeded when cold boot left them at 0x000000). **Next step**: disassemble 0x0821A3, add missing block as seed, retranspile, and re-probe. Artifacts: `probe-phase25r-createreal-errsp.mjs`, `phase25r-createreal-errsp-report.md`.
- ❌ **Phase 25R — ParseInp errSP — INFORMATIVE FAIL (errNo=0x88 DISCOVERED)** — Same 0x082be2/0x084711-0x084723 parser loop as sessions 73/75, hit max_steps=500000. BUT: errNo=0x88 was written (NEW finding — error code was set via a non-longjmp mechanism). errSP stayed at seeded value 0xD1A869 (longjmp never triggered). OPS pointer moved backwards from 0xD1A881→0xD1A877 (parser consumed some bytes then backed up). OP1=[ff 58 00 00 00 00 00 00 00] (garbage). **Key insight**: the error code 0x88 is set during parser execution but doesn't trigger the longjmp at 0x061DB2 — possibly written to errNo by a TRY/CATCH-style mechanism inside the parser that catches and handles its own errors without unwinding. The parser loop is stuck in VAT search code (0x082be2 is in the Create allocator region per session 77's disassembly). Artifacts: `probe-phase25r-parseinp-errsp.mjs`, `phase25r-parseinp-errsp-report.md`.
- Golden regression 26/26 PASS post-session. All 3 Codex dispatches succeeded on first attempt.

### Completed (session 76)
- ✅ **Phase 25Q — InvOP1S PASS** — InvOP1S(0x07CA06) confirmed as negate operation (same as InvOP1Sc). Test 1: 7.0→-7.0 exact (sign byte 0x00→0x80). Test 2: -3.5→3.5 exact (sign byte 0x80→0x00). Static disassembly reveals InvOP1Sc(0x07CA02) starts with `call 0x07CA27` (conditioning) then falls into InvOP1S, while InvOP1S calls `0x07F7BD` directly (the actual negation). Codex succeeded on first attempt. Total validated FP primitives: **15** (FPAdd, FPSub, FPMult, FPDiv, FPSquare, SqRoot, Sin, Cos, Tan, LnX, TenX, CpOP1OP2, FPRecip, InvOP1Sc, InvOP1S). Artifacts: `probe-phase25q-invop1s.mjs`, report.
- ✅ **Phase 25Q — Error handler 0x061DB2 disassembly — RESOLVED (LONGJMP)** — Static disassembly of the TI-OS error convergence point. **0x061DB2 is a classic setjmp/longjmp**: (1) `ld (errNo=0xD008DF), a` stores error code, (2) `call 0x03E1B4` interrupt-safe cleanup wrapper (saves A to scratch 0xD00542, checks `ld a,i / jp pe`, DI, calls 0x03E187, restores EI state), (3) clears 4 IY-offset flag bits (IY+75 bit7, IY+18 bit2, IY+36 bit4, IY+73 bit1), (4) **`ld sp, (errSP=0xD008E0)` — THE LONGJMP**, (5) `pop af; ret` — returns to whatever address was saved at the errSP frame. **Does NOT call DispErrorScreen (0x062160)**. The 0x58c35b "crash" is caused by uninitialized errSP (0xFF fill) → garbage SP → garbage return address. DispErrorScreen is called by the recovery point (the "setjmp" side), not by the error handler itself. Gap region 0x061D80-0x061DB1 confirmed as tail of error dispatch table (13 more entries with error codes 0x28, 0x2E, 0xAB, 0xAC, 0xAF, 0x2F, 0x30, 0x31, 0xB4, 0x9F, 0xB5, 0x36). Codex timed out; Sonnet fallback succeeded. Artifacts: `probe-phase25q-error-handler.mjs`, report.
- ✅ **Phase 25Q — CreateReal entry 0x082386 disassembly — RESOLVED** — Extended disassembly of 0x082340-0x0823F0 region. **Key findings**: (1) 0x082386 is simply `jp 0x0822D9` — a shared Create allocator dispatcher. CreateReal at 0x08238A sets A=0(RealObj), HL=9(size), then `jr 0x082386 → jp 0x0822D9`. (2) CreateCplx at 0x082380 sets A=0x0C, HL=18(=2×9). (3) The type-check at 0x08239C (checking 0x5D/0x24/0x3A/0x72) is a SEPARATE routine that runs AFTER the allocator returns, not part of CreateReal's entry path. Those values are list/string/program/complex NAME PREFIX bytes, not type codes. (4) **0xD00619 = OP4** (confirmed from ti84pceg.inc). Bit 3 of OP4 tested post-allocation to tag complex entries with 0x0C. (5) **ADDRESS CORRECTIONS**: progPtr=0xD0259D (not 0xD01C00 as previously guessed), pTemp=0xD0259A, OPBase=0xD02590, pTempCnt=0xD02596, symTable=0xD3FFFF. The SYMBOLS map in previous probes had wrong addresses. (6) Next target: disassemble the shared allocator at 0x0822D9. Codex timed out; Sonnet fallback succeeded. Artifacts: `probe-phase25q-createreal-entry.mjs`, report.
- Golden regression 26/26 PASS post-session. 1 Codex + 2 Sonnet fallback dispatches (2 Codex timed out on static disassembly tasks).

ParseInp advanced 197 blocks through real token dispatch (0x099xxx → 0x09bxxx → 0x080090 → 0x09bae3 → 0x061d1a → 0x061db2 → 0x03e1b4 → 0x03e1ca → 0x061dba → 0x58c35b). The parser internally calls into the 0x080090 VAT region which triggers the same error path as CreateReal. OP1 untouched. **KEY INSIGHT**: ParseInp's internal variable lookup hits the same missing-VAT-state issue as CreateReal. Both need VAT head pointers (progPtr/pTemp) and possibly a correctly initialized VAT structure to avoid the error dispatch. Artifacts: `probe-phase25p-parseinp-ops.mjs`, report.
- ✅ **Phase 25P — VAT disassembly (KEY DISCOVERY)** — Static disassembly of CreateReal entry 0x08238A and crash paths 0x061D1A/0x061D3E/0x03E1B4/0x03E1CA. **0x061D1A-0x061D7E is the TI-OS error code dispatch table**, NOT stack corruption. Every entry: `ld a, <error_code>; jr 0x061db2`. CreateReal at 0x08239c does `ld a, (0xD005F9)` (OP1+1 = type byte), compares against 0x5D (list), 0x24, 0x3A, 0x72 — if none match → `jp nz, 0x061d46` → error 0x8F. Our session-73 probe set OP1[1]=0x41 (name "A") when the code expects a TYPE byte at that position. CreateReal also reads 0xD00619 after the type check (bit 3 test). The 0x03E1B4 subroutine is an interrupt-safe scratch routine using 0xD00542 as temporary. IY+18 (0xD00092) is touched by `set 2, (iy+18)`. No IX-offset reads found in any disassembled range. Sonnet fallback used (Codex timed out). Artifacts: `probe-phase25p-vat-disasm.mjs`, report.
- Golden regression 26/26 PASS post-session. 3 Codex + 1 Sonnet fallback dispatches.

(2) `0x099B18` calls ChkFindSym(0x08383D), stores DE into asm_ram(0xD00687) as scratch, then WRITES begPC(0xD02317) and curPC(0xD0231A) — these are outputs, not inputs, explaining why seeding them in session 73 had no effect. (3) `0x09BEED` reads `OPS (0xD02593)` — this is the critical input pointer. Loop at 0x084711 reads OP1+1(0xD005F9) as a byte compare, not a pointer fetch. **Conclusion**: next ParseInp probe should seed OPS=0xD02593. Artifacts: `probe-phase25o-parseinp-helpers.mjs`, report.

### Completed (session 73)
- ✅ **Phase 25L — FP edge pack (FPSub, FPSquare, CpOP1OP2)** — Three probes mirroring 25I-fpadd template. **FPSub(5-3)=2.0** exact (OP1 `00 80 20 00 00 00 00 00 00`), **FPSquare(7²)=49.0** exact (OP1 `00 81 49 00 00 00 00 00 00`), **CpOP1OP2** 3-case probe confirms standard TI flag convention: lt (3<5) → F=0xA3 (C=1 Z=0), eq (5=5) → F=0x42 (C=0 Z=1), gt (7>2) → F=0x02 (C=0 Z=0). All three cases produce distinct flag states. Artifacts: `probe-phase25l-{fpsub,fpsquare,cpop1op2}.mjs`, 3 reports. All 3 PASS.

Slot at 0xD012A8 transitioned from `ff × 9` → `00 81 42 00 00 00 00 00 00` = 42.0 exact. Round-trip via Rcl_StatVar with OP1 cleared to 0xFF returned 42.0 exact (diff=0). First validated STORE direction for stat vars — establishes the full read/write pattern for all stat variables. Artifacts: `probe-phase25m-sto-statvar.mjs`, `phase25m-sto-statvar-report.md`. PASS.

VAT routines need stack/IX setup our postInitState doesn't provide — possibly seeding VAT head pointers (progPtr/pTemp) or correcting IX.
